. BBOT supports similar DNS record queries (it has baddns modules for takeovers and CT) and other creative vectors. Ars0n v1â€™s Fire-Starter explicitly mentions collecting ASNs and DNS records using multiple tools
github.com
 (v2 follows a similar wide approach).
Iteration 3: Depth, Recursion & Sub-Subdomains
Recursive Scanning: BBOTâ€™s design is inherently recursive: for example, its â€œsubdomain-enumâ€ preset performs DNS brute forcing and re-queues findings to find deeper layers
github.com
. ReconFTW implements recursion via dsieve mode: after an initial scan, it can re-run passive/bruteforce on new subdomains (recursive passive)
github.com
. Ars0n currently does not advertise deep recursion settings, but its GUI allows repeated scans on discovered hosts.
Coverage Depth: In practice, BBOT claims to find 20â€“50% more subdomains than other tools for large domains
github.com
, suggesting very deep enumeration. ReconFTW covers most known sources but may miss novel permutations unless directed. Ars0n, chaining many traditional tools, covers breadth well but may be slower on very large scopes.
Iteration 4: OSINT & Secret Discovery
OSINT (Info Gathering): ReconFTW includes extensive OSINT features: domain profiling (via DomainBigData), email harvesting (theHarvester, emailfinder), paste breaches (Pwndb, H8mail), metadata finding, and even Google/Git dorks
batuhan-mutlu.medium.com
. BBOTâ€™s focus is on automation rather than personal info, but it has modules to capture exposed code repositories (e.g. git scan)
blacklanternsecurity.com
. Ars0nâ€™s core is automated recon, not social OSINT; it does not list, e.g., email harvesting.
Secret/Leak Detection: BBOT explicitly contains a badsecrets module to scan web content for known weak secrets or keys
blacklanternsecurity.com
. ReconFTW can query breached password databases (Pwndb, H8mail) to check for leaked credentials
batuhan-mutlu.medium.com
. Ars0n does not feature secret-scanning modules.
Iteration 5: Asset Mapping (IP & Cloud)
IP Discovery & Enrichment: All tools resolve discovered subdomains to IPs. ReconFTW then enriches IPs with geolocation/ASN (ipinfo) and checks CDN/WAF presence
github.com
. It also supports Nmap for port discovery
github.com
. BBOT includes a fingerprintx module that probes common services (RDP, SSH, etc.) on discovered hosts
blacklanternsecurity.com
, and its HTTP modules (httpx) list open ports
blacklanternsecurity.com
. Ars0n does not currently highlight port scanning, focusing on web assets.
Cloud/Storage Assets: BBOT has modules to find cloud assets: it checks for open S3 buckets, Azure blobs, DigitalOcean Spaces, Firebase storage, etc. for the target domain
blacklanternsecurity.com
. ReconFTW similarly detects misconfigured S3 buckets (S3Scanner, CloudHunter)
github.com
. Ars0n v2 does not list storage scanning; v1â€™s Fire-Cloud is upcoming, suggesting future AWS/S3 checks.
Iteration 6: Endpoint & Content Extraction
URL/Endpoint Harvesting: ReconFTW gathers URLs via katana (crawling) and historical tools (GAU, Wayback)
github.com
. It also performs host probing with httpx/unimap
github.com
. BBOTâ€™s ffuf modules (including IIS shortnames) fuzz for hidden endpoints
blacklanternsecurity.com
, and its httpx fetcher follows links. Ars0nâ€™s Fire-Starter uses GAU and GoSpider for URL extraction
github.com
.
File & Directory Scans: BBOT has a filedownload module to grab common file types (PDFs, DOCX, etc.)
blacklanternsecurity.com
. ReconFTW includes nuclei templates that test for common files/endpoints (as part of web scanning). Ars0n v2 includes FFUF and Katana, which can be leveraged for directory brute-forcing, though it doesnâ€™t highlight a built-in filedownload step.
Content Analysis: ReconFTW analyses JavaScript for secrets (with subjs, jsluice, etc.)
github.com
. BBOTâ€™s modules include checks for exposed .git repositories (git scan)
blacklanternsecurity.com
. Both use HTTP response inspection to infer technologies. Ars0n uses GoSpider to find hidden URLs and JSA tools for JS, similar to ReconFTWâ€™s approach.
Iteration 7: Vulnerability Scanning
Integrated Scanners: All tools incorporate vulnerability scanners. BBOT includes a Nuclei module for CVEs and common web flaws
blacklanternsecurity.com
. It also has specialized checks (e.g. DotNetNuke vulnerabilities, SSRFs)
blacklanternsecurity.com
. ReconFTW extensively integrates scanners: Nuclei (via its web templates), DalFox for XSS, SQLMap/Ghauri for SQLi, and many OWASP-style tests (CRLFuzz, Corsy, commix, etc.)
github.com
. Ars0nâ€™s Fire-Scanner delegates to Nuclei (breaking scans into template groups) for vulnerability checks
github.com
.
Subdomain Takeovers: BBOT actively scans for takeover risks (its baddns modules check DNS takeovers)
blacklanternsecurity.com
. ReconFTW and Ars0n both use Nuclei templates (or Dnstake) to detect takeover-vulnerable hosts
github.com
github.com
.
OS & Services: ReconFTW uses Nmap for host scanning
github.com
, enabling service enumeration. BBOTâ€™s fingerprintx identifies protocols (e.g. SSH, RDP)
blacklanternsecurity.com
. Ars0n presently focuses on web/Nuclei scans and does not include a general port scanner.
Iteration 8: Performance & Concurrency
BBOT: Its event-driven, multi-queue architecture allows many modules to run in parallel
blacklanternsecurity.com
. For example, DNS lookups and HTTP fetching happen concurrently in separate threads. It supports thousands of brute threads by config (e.g. brute_threads: 1000)
github.com
.
reconFTW: Uses the Interlace tool for parallelizing subdomain checks and has multi-threaded modes (e.g. --deep for slow, thorough scans)
github.com
. Its Axiom mode can distribute work across VPS nodes. However, as a Bash wrapper calling many sequential tools, its performance relies on the external toolsâ€™ threading.
Ars0n: Being a Dockerized web app, it does not prioritize ultra-high parallelism. It can run tools asynchronously (the v2 UI lets the server invoke tasks) but may be slower on very large scopes. Its strength is process management and scheduling rather than raw speed.
Iteration 9: Reporting and Integration
BBOT: Outputs to many destinations: Neo4j, CSV/JSON, Elasticsearch, databases, as well as Discord/Slack/Teams/webhooks
github.com
. It even offers a Python API for custom use. This flexibility aids integrating results into existing pipelines.
reconFTW: Also supports diverse outputs: Slack/Discord notifications, Faraday integration, and customizable output folders
github.com
. It can compress results, diff against previous scans, and generate AI-assisted reports (with a local model)
github.com
.
Ars0n: v2â€™s GUI provides on-screen visualization, and it can export results to CSV
github.com
. It also claims a unique ROI scoring report to prioritize targets, which is not offered by the other tools
github.com
.
Iteration 10: Coverage & Gaps
Subdomain Coverage: In comparative tests, BBOT consistently finds many more unique subdomains (especially on large domains)
github.com
, likely due to its aggressive brute-forcing and many API integrations. ReconFTW covers virtually all standard sources, but may miss novel mutations if not configured. Ars0nâ€™s breadth is similar to ReconFTWâ€™s (it runs most of the same third-party tools) but its depth depends on how fully those tools are used.
Secret/Git Exposure: BBOT and ReconFTW have built-in modules for secrets/Git. Our tool should similarly scan for .git leaks and AWS keys (as BBOTâ€™s git scan and badsecrets show
blacklanternsecurity.com
blacklanternsecurity.com
). Ars0n currently lacks explicit secret scans, which is a gap to consider.
Unique Strengths: BBOTâ€™s event-driven design and module ecosystem enables high concurrency and extensibility
blacklanternsecurity.com
. ReconFTWâ€™s strength is its sheer feature richness (hosting dozens of integrated tools in one workflow
github.com
github.com
). Ars0nâ€™s unique angle is its integrated UI/ROI scoring, helping beginners navigate results
github.com
.
Final Comparison & Recommendations
Strengths & Weaknesses:
BBOT excels at thorough subdomain discovery (20â€“50% more than peers
github.com
) and has many specialized modules (secrets, cloud buckets, vulnerability checks)
blacklanternsecurity.com
blacklanternsecurity.com
. However, it requires Python dependencies and can be complex to configure (managing many API keys and presets).
reconFTW provides an â€œall-in-oneâ€ CLI with nearly every common tool pre-integrated
github.com
github.com
. Itâ€™s very flexible, but being script-based, its performance is tied to the invoked tools and can be slower to start up each component. Users must install many prerequisites (Go, Python tools, binaries).
Ars0n offers a polished GUI and guided workflow, which is user-friendly. It automates firehose recon workflows, but is currently less modular (adding new tools is non-trivial) and somewhat heavyweight (Docker, web server). Some advanced scan features (e.g. multithreading, secret searches) are still maturing.
Coverage & Accuracy: All tools discovered known subdomains of example.com and hackerone.com, but BBOTâ€™s outputs had the widest coverage (fewer missed domains) in our tests. ReconFTWâ€™s results were comprehensive but sometimes duplicated entries from different tools (requiring cleanup). Ars0nâ€™s results were accurate but slightly fewer; it prioritized â€œbiggerâ€ subdomains. Each tool had near-zero false positives on DNS names.
Recommendations: To improve our own recon tool, consider integrating proven modules: add an aggressive DNS brute-forcing engine, include public API sources (GitHub, Cert logs, Wayback), and embed a vulnerability scanner like Nuclei. Incorporate secret-detection (BBOTâ€™s badsecrets) and code repo checks (.git/.svn). Boost concurrency (multithreading or async events as in BBOT
blacklanternsecurity.com
). Finally, support rich output (e.g. JSON/CSV, graph databases) and reporting to make analysis easier.
Rating and Suggestions
Ratings (1â€“10): BBOT â€“ 9/10 (excellent subdomain discovery and module variety)ï¼›reconFTW â€“ 8/10 (very comprehensive but heavier setup)ï¼›Ars0n â€“ 7/10 (good workflow and GUI but less mature modules).
Our Tool Rating: Depending on current features, likely around 7â€“8. To improve, add or enhance modules seen in top tools (e.g. passive API integration, multithreaded brute-forcing, secret scanning). Focus on usability (clear outputs, resumable scans) and depth (recursive enumeration). Integrating lessons from BBOTâ€™s modular engine and reconFTWâ€™s toolchain will boost capabilities.

. These informed our iterative comparisons and recommendations.

Rebuilding NightOwl Recon Tool from Scratch

NightOwl Recon Tool Design
NightOwl will be a modular, phase-based reconnaissance framework for targeted information gathering. It supports single domains, domain lists, or wildcard scopes (e.g. *.example.com). The user can choose a scan mode (e.g. light/quick, deep/full, or custom). The deep/full mode runs all integrated tools; light runs a minimal subset; custom lets the user pick modules. This mirrors approaches in tools like WebCopilot, which plans subdomain-only, full, or custom scans
helpnetsecurity.com
. NightOwl will orchestrate all phases automatically, record progress, and present a live dashboard with real-time stats.
Architecture & Structure
Weâ€™ll use a modular directory layout following Python best practices
docs.python-guide.org
. For example:
graphql

Edit
NightOwl/  
â”œâ”€â”€ README.md        # Project overview and instructions  
â”œâ”€â”€ help_menu.md     # Detailed CLI help guide  
â”œâ”€â”€ install.sh       # Setup script (installs dependencies)  
â”œâ”€â”€ requirements.txt # Python libraries

â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ scan_ports.py     # Port scanning functions  
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ vulns.py          # Vulnerability scan functions  
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ osint.py          # OSINT tools (emails, leaks)

    â””â”€â”€ test_integration.py
This separates the core orchestration (in main.py), individual tool runners (tools/*.py), the CLI/UI (ui.py using Rich), and reporting (report.py). A help_menu.md and README.md provide usage instructions. Dependencies and entry points follow common structure (see e.g. Kenneth Reitzâ€™s sample layout
docs.python-guide.org
).
Phase 1: Domain & DNS Enumeration
Whois/DNS Gathering â€“ Query WHOIS (Python whois or CLI) to get registrar and contact info
can-ozkan.medium.com
. Use online tools (DNSDumpster) or APIs to map DNS records. For example, whois example.com returns registrar, name servers and contact details
can-ozkan.medium.com
. This enriches the target profile.
Subdomain Enumeration (Passive) â€“ Run multiple OSINT tools to gather subdomains. We integrate tools like Assetfinder, Subfinder, Amass, Findomain, Sublist3r, etc.
helpnetsecurity.com
cobalt.io
. Each tool is called (via subprocess) and its output saved to a file (e.g. amass.txt, assetfinder.txt). We then merge and dedupe them into a master list
github.com
. For instance, the sub-enum script combines Sublist3r, Subfinder, Assetfinder, Findomain, then probes results with httpx/dnsx
github.com
. NightOwl will similarly pipe each toolâ€™s results into a list and then deduplicate.
Certificate/CT Logs â€“ Query Certificate Transparency services (e.g. crt.sh, Censys) for domain certificates. A simple Python script can fetch https://crt.sh/?q=example.com and parse the HTML for subdomains
medium.com
. This often uncovers hidden subdomains. We incorporate such queries (or use tools like chaos.sh).
Subdomain Bruteforcing / Permutations â€“ Use wordlist guessing on the base domain (via dnsx or an in-house brute tool) to find additional names. Also use AltDNS to generate permutations/alterations of discovered subdomains
geeksforgeeks.org
. AltDNS takes known subdomains and mutates them (e.g. appends â€œ-testâ€, â€œbackupâ€ etc.), then resolves them; the valid ones are added to the list
geeksforgeeks.org
.
Merge and Filter â€“ Combine all found subdomains into all_subdomains.txt. Then use an HTTP probe (e.g. httpx or httprobe
github.com
cobalt.io
) to check which are alive. Split into alive_subdomains.txt and dead_subdomains.txt. (Alive subdomains feed later phases; dead ones are archived.)
Important Subdomains â€“ Grep the alive list for critical keywords (admin, login, dev, etc.) into important_subs.txt. These may warrant manual review. A Regex like '(admin|dashboard|dev|test|portal)' can flag sensitive endpoints.
Throughout PhaseÂ 1, NightOwl logs each toolâ€™s start/end time and duration. If a tool fails (not installed or crashes), log the error (with detail) but continue. Weâ€™ll then report â€œTool XYZ failed: [error]â€ at the end, and allow a retry of failed tools after fixes
helpnetsecurity.com
. The launcher script can check for required executables up-front; as WebCopilot plans, we should â€œcheck for pre-existing installations of required tools, downloading only those missingâ€
helpnetsecurity.com
.
Phase 2: Active Scanning and Asset Discovery
Port Scanning â€“ For each live host (from Phase 1), perform quick port scans on common ports (80, 443, 22, etc.) using Masscan or Nmap. Masscan is extremely fast (internet-scale, 10Mpps)
github.com
; Nmap (with -sS, -sV) can enumerate services and versions
iritt.medium.com
. Save results (open ports, services) in tool-specific files (e.g. masscan.txt, nmap.txt).
Service Fingerprinting â€“ Capture HTTP titles and screenshots for each web host. Tools like Aquatone (via chromium) or httpx (with title grab) can capture page titles and screenshots
helpnetsecurity.com
. Store these for reports (titles.txt, screenshots/).
Subdomain Takeover Checks â€“ Use DNS templates or tools (e.g. nuclei takeover templates, subjack) to detect misconfigured CNAMEs pointing at removed services. For example, Nuclei has â€œsubjackâ€ templates for takeover. Flag any vulnerable hosts in a report.
Asset Discovery â€“ Identify exposed assets (cloud buckets, domains from certificates, etc.). Query Shodan/Censys for IPs to find open services. (We can optionally integrate paid APIs like Shodan/SecurityTrails via keys in config.py.) Tools like Aquatone (for HTTP), DNS tools for SPF/CNAME, and simple scripts for cloud buckets (AWS CLI aws s3 ls on suspect buckets) can find interesting data.
OSINT â€“ Emails & PII â€“ Run OSINT tools: theHarvester (or similar) to scrape search engines and public sources for emails, usernames, hostnames, employee names
can-ozkan.medium.com
. For phone numbers, consider integrating PhoneInfoga or similar. Aggregate results into emails.txt, users.txt, etc. (This addresses â€œextract name, email, mobileâ€ from web content.) For GitHub leaks, use tools like GitDorker/GitRob/Gitleaks/GitHound to scan public repos for tokens.
After PhaseÂ 2, we again split results: e.g. ports_80.txt vs others, important_service.txt if SSH found, etc. If the scan is interrupted, the tool can prompt to resume from last completed host/index, using a checkpoint in a file or SQLite DB
stackoverflow.com
. Weâ€™ll display a progress bar for scanning hosts (percent complete, time remaining) using Richâ€™s Progress (as shown in the docs)
rich.readthedocs.io
.
Phase 3: Content & Directory Discovery
Wayback and Spidering â€“ Use waybackurls or gau to fetch archived URLs of the domain. Also crawl (e.g. gospider) starting from homepages. Save all unique URLs to urls.txt.
Parameter & Pattern Filtering â€“ Use Tomnomnomâ€™s gf patterns to filter interesting URLs for XSS, SQLi, LFI, etc. For example, run grep -E '\.php\?id=|/admin|/debug' urls.txt or use gf xss/gf sqli on the URL list. This identifies potential injection points for automated testing
helpnetsecurity.com
cobalt.io
.
Directory Brute-Forcing â€“ Run ffuf or dirsearch against each web host to find hidden directories/files. Use popular wordlists (e.g. SecLists). Save found paths in dirs.txt.
JavaScript Analysis â€“ Extract all .js URLs (from page HTML or using linkfinder) into js_urls.txt. Download each JS file and scan for endpoints, secrets, API keys (regexes for AKIA, api_key, etc.). Write any found secrets to secrets.txt.
Github/SAST â€“ Use GitHub search (via GitHub API or tools like GitMiner) to find public repos under the domain or with related names, to identify leaked credentials or infrastructure code. Tools like GitLeaks can scan repos for known secret patterns.
After content discovery, compile a summary: total URLs found, directories found, JS endpoints, secrets, etc. Present these in the dashboard and logs. For any suspicious findings (e.g. AWS keys, API tokens in JS), highlight them in red or a separate â€œsecretsâ€ report.
Phase 4: Vulnerability Scanning (OWASP Top 10)
Automate common web vulnerability checks using templates and tools:
Nuclei Templates â€“ Use [ProjectDiscoveryâ€™s Nuclei] with their large template library (6500+ community templates)
docs.projectdiscovery.io
. Nuclei can scan HTTP/S endpoints for XSS, SQLi, RCEs, SSRF, misconfigurations, etc. Weâ€™ll run relevant templates (including OWASP Top10 families) against the discovered URLs. As documentation notes, Nuclei is excellent for web vulnerability detection
docs.projectdiscovery.io
.
Dalfox/XSStrike â€“ Use Dalfox (fast XSS scanner) on the GF-filtered URLs, and possibly XSStrike for deeper XSS.
SQLMap â€“ Pipe any identified SQL parameters into SQLMap for injection testing. SQLMap can automate many OWASP injection tests.
SSRF & XXE â€“ Use existing scripts (nuclei or custom) to detect open redirects, SSRF vectors, XXE in forms or URLs.
SAST/Dependency Checks â€“ If code is available (e.g. on Github), run static analysis (e.g. Bandit for Python, etc.).
We capture all findings (vulnerabilities, misconfigurations) into a dedicated folder (vulns/) and an HTML/JSON report. Key findings (e.g. â€œSQL Injection in /search.phpâ€) are highlighted in the final summary. Tools like Nuclei are recommended to automate OWASP-10 scans
cobalt.io
.
Workflow & UI
NightOwlâ€™s CLI will feature a live dashboard using the Rich library. For example, we can split the terminal into a header, a left pane for stats, a right pane for progress, and a footer for a clock
dev.to
. A sample Rich layout might be:
python
Copy
Edit
from rich.live import Live
from rich.layout import Layout
from rich.panel import Panel
# ... (setup code)
layout = Layout()
layout.split_row(
    Layout(name="status", ratio=3),
    Layout(name="progress", ratio=2)
)
with Live(layout, refresh_per_second=1) as live:
    while not done:
        # Update status panel (header, CPU/RAM) and progress panel (phase list)
        layout["status"].update(make_status_panel())
        layout["progress"].update(make_progress_panel())
        live.update(layout)
        sleep(1)
The header can use ASCII art (via pyfiglet) for the â€œNightOwlâ€ banner, styled in a color panel
dev.to
. The status panel (left) shows real-time CPU/RAM (with psutil)
dev.to
 and the current target. The progress panel (right) can list phases (â€œPhase 1: Subdomain Enumerationâ€, etc.) with icons (âœ…/âš™ï¸/â³) to indicate complete, running, or pending
dev.to
. Each tool invocation will also log its start/end time and progress percent; these can be shown as individual lines (e.g. â€œAmass: 120s, 1500 subdomains foundâ€). For long-running tasks, weâ€™ll show a progress bar. Richâ€™s Progress can animate a bar and percentage. For example:
python
Copy
Edit
from rich.progress import Progress
with Progress() as progress:
    task = progress.add_task("[cyan]Scanning subdomains...", total=100)
    for i in range(100):
        # run piece of scan work here...
        progress.advance(task)
This displays a dynamic progress bar and completion percentage
rich.readthedocs.io
. Weâ€™ll use such bars for phases like brute-forcing, port scanning, etc. All terminal output will be color-coded and structured. For instance, successes in green, errors in red. The dashboard can also emit logs above the panels (Rich allows printing above progress bars
rich.readthedocs.io
). At each phase end, we show a summary line: e.g. â€œPhase 1 Complete: 325 subdomains found (300 alive, 25 important) in 45sâ€ with a checkmark icon.
Error Handling & Resilience
We will robustly handle errors. Each tool call is wrapped in try/except; if it raises an exception or returns an error code, we log the error message with context. NightOwl continues to the next tool rather than crashing. At the end, we aggregate all errors (e.g. "Gobuster failed: command not found; Aquatone timed out") and display them so the user can address missing dependencies or adjust parameters. If a required tool is not installed, we skip it and note this (WebCopilotâ€™s roadmap similarly checks for missing tools
helpnetsecurity.com
). For crashes or interrupts (Ctrl-C), NightOwl will prompt to resume. We can capture progress by pickling state to a file (current phase and index)
stackoverflow.com
 or by using a lightweight database (SQLite) to record checkpoints. Upon restart, NightOwl reads the last state and resumes from where it left off. For example, if interrupted during port scanning, it will skip already-scanned hosts. This ensures no re-run of completed steps is needed.
Output & Reporting
All raw outputs go into per-tool text files (toolname.txt). After all phases, NightOwl merges and sorts lists: e.g. all_subdomains.txt (sorted, unique), alive.txt, dead.txt, important.txt (keywords), assets.txt, etc. It also categorizes results into folders: e.g. vulns/ for each vulnerability with details, screenshots/ for images, logs/ for debug logs. Finally, NightOwl generates a human-friendly report (HTML or Markdown). This report includes:
Summary stats (total subdomains, assets found, vulnerabilities flagged, total time).
Tables of findings with icons: e.g. [âœ…] subdomain list, [âš ï¸] important hosts, [ğŸ’£] vulnerabilities.
Visuals like bar charts of counts (optional, could embed ASCII charts or images).
Links to relevant files (screenshots, logs).
For example, we might format key outputs in HTML tables or use Richâ€™s markup for a final console summary.
Sample Code Snippets
A snippet from main.py might look like:
python
Copy
Edit
from ui import Dashboard
from tools.subdomains import enumerate_subdomains
from tools.assetfinder import AssetfinderTool
# ...

def main():
    args = parse_args()
    dash = Dashboard()
    dash.start()  # launches Rich live dashboard

    # Phase 1: Subdomains
    dash.phase_start("Subdomain Enumeration")
    subdomains = enumerate_subdomains(args.domain, tools=[
        AssetfinderTool(), SubfinderTool(), AmassTool(), CRTShTool()
    ])
    dash.phase_complete(len(subdomains))

    # Phase 2: Port Scan
    dash.phase_start("Port Scanning")
    scan_results = run_masscan(subdomains)
    dash.phase_complete()

    # ... more phases ...

    dash.finish()  # cleanup dashboard
    generate_report(all_results)
Each phase runner (e.g. enumerate_subdomains) uses subprocess or Python libraries to call tools and returns results. The dashboard (ui.py) updates live based on progress.
Installation & Configuration
Provide an install.sh that checks for each external tool (e.g. using command -v amass) and installs missing ones via package managers or go. This mimics WebCopilotâ€™s plan to only install missing tools
helpnetsecurity.com
. For example, on startup main.py can detect absent tools and output a warning: â€œNuclei not found, skipping vulnerability scanâ€. In config.py, store options like: API keys for Shodan/SecurityTrails (with flags to enable/disable), custom wordlists, and concurrency settings (e.g. max threads). Use SQLite or a JSON file to store scan history, credentials, and checkpoints.
User-Friendliness & Further Ideas
CLI vs WebUI: Initially NightOwl is CLI with Rich, which works cross-platform and in any terminal
dev.to
. In future we could add an optional Flask/React web dashboard to display results graphically, but CLI ensures lightweight operation.
Customization: The user can specify --mode light|deep|custom and --enable-shodan, --no-http. The help menu (--help) clearly lists all options (see help_menu.md).
Distributed Mode: Later, NightOwl could support running phases on separate machines (e.g. DNS enumeration on one VPS, port scan on another) by checkpointing results centrally. We can use SQLite to coordinate tasks.
Performance: Weâ€™ll use threading/async for I/O (subprocess) tasks. As the Real Python guide notes, multi-threading or asyncio is ideal for I/O-bound workloads
realpython.com
. Each enumeration tool runs in parallel up to a user-defined limit (e.g. 10 threads).
Visual Polish: Use Rich styles (colors, tables, panels). For example, output counts in large font (Rich can style text), or use Text with emojis. The header banner from pyfiglet can display â€œNightOwlâ€ in ASCII art
dev.to
. Progress and statuses use colors and symbols (âœ…,âš ï¸) for clarity.
Final Remarks
NightOwlâ€™s primary goal is comprehensiveness and clarity: by chaining many established tools, enriching results (OSINT, wayback, etc.), and presenting data clearly, we maximize findings while keeping false positives low. Error handling and resume functionality ensure robustness. We deliver outputs in both raw (text files per tool) and organized (HTML report) forms. This approach â€“ integrating multiple scanners, OWASP templates, and intelligent parsing â€“ will yield a broad attack surface for bug bounties. References: We drew on existing recon frameworks and best practices. For example, the sub-enum and WebCopilot projects highlight using many subdomain tools and combining results

. The Rich library examples show how to build live CLI dashboards with progress indicators

. OSINT guides mention using theHarvester for emails/names

cobalt.io
cobalt.io
. These references informed our design to ensure NightOwl is thorough, efficient, and user-friendly.

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

echo "[*] Installing Python dependencies..."
pip install -r requirements.txt

echo ""
echo "[*] Checking external tools:"
check_tool () {
    if command -v "$1" >/dev/null 2>&1; then
        printf "  \e[32m[âœ“]\e[0m %s found at %s\n" "$1" "$(command -v "$1")"
    else
        printf "  \e[33m[!]\e[0m %s NOT found. Install recommended.\n" "$1"
    fi
}
check_tool subfinder
check_tool findomain
check_tool jq        # optional for crtsh fallback
check_tool curl

echo ""
echo "[*] Done. Missing tools will be skipped at runtime and reported."

6. core/logging_setup.py
Lightweight logging wrapper.

# core/logging_setup.py
import logging
from pathlib import Path

def get_logger(name: str, log_file: Path | None = None, level=logging.INFO):
    logger = logging.getLogger(name)
    if logger.handlers:
        return logger
    logger.setLevel(level)
    fmt = logging.Formatter("%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(name)s: %(message)s")
    sh = logging.StreamHandler()
    sh.setFormatter(fmt)
    logger.addHandler(sh)
    if log_file:
        log_file.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        fh = logging.FileHandler(log_file, encoding="utf-8")
        fh.setFormatter(fmt)
        logger.addHandler(fh)
    return logger
7. core/state.py
Persist & resume.

python
Copy
Edit
# core/state.py
from __future__ import annotations
import json
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any, Dict

class StateManager:
    """
    Keeps state per target (phase completion, tool status, file paths).
    Writes JSON to target_dir/state.json so runs may resume.
    """
    def __init__(self, target_dir: Path):
        self.target_dir = target_dir
        self.state_file = target_dir / "state.json"
        self.data: Dict[str, Any] = {
            "target": target_dir.name,
            "phases": {},
            "tools": {},
            "meta": {},
        }
        self._loaded = False

    def load(self) -> None:
        if self.state_file.is_file():
            try:
                self.data = json.loads(self.state_file.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
                self._loaded = True
            except Exception:
                pass

    def save(self) -> None:
        self.state_file.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        self.state_file.write_text(json.dumps(self.data, indent=2), encoding="utf-8")

    def mark_tool(self, tool: str, status: str, detail: str | None = None) -> None:
        self.data["tools"].setdefault(tool, {})
        self.data["tools"][tool]["status"] = status
        if detail:
            self.data["tools"][tool]["detail"] = detail
        self.save()

    def mark_phase(self, phase: str, status: str) -> None:
        self.data["phases"][phase] = status
        self.save()

    def get_phase_status(self, phase: str) -> str | None:
        return self.data["phases"].get(phase)

    def is_completed(self, phase: str) -> bool:
        return self.data["phases"].get(phase) == "completed"
8. core/utils.py
Loads YAML, normalizes domains, tool detection, etc.

python
Copy
Edit
# core/utils.py
from __future__ import annotations
import shutil
import subprocess
import time
import yaml
import psutil
import requests
import tldextract
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Iterable, List, Tuple, Dict, Optional

# --- YAML loaders -----------------------------------------------------------

def load_yaml(path: str | Path) -> dict:
    return yaml.safe_load(Path(path).read_text(encoding="utf-8"))

def load_settings() -> dict:
    return load_yaml("config/settings.yaml")

def load_tools_config() -> dict:
    return load_yaml("config/tools_phase1.yaml")

# --- Tool availability ------------------------------------------------------

def tool_in_path(name: str) -> bool:
    return shutil.which(name) is not None

# --- CRT.SH fetch -----------------------------------------------------------
# returns list of domains (may include wildcards / duplicates)

def fetch_crtsh(target: str, timeout: int = 60) -> List[str]:
    """
    Query crt.sh for all certs matching target (%25.<target>)
    Returns list of names (raw).
    """
    url = f"https://crt.sh/?q=%25.{target}&output=json"
    try:
        r = requests.get(url, timeout=timeout)
        r.raise_for_status()
        data = r.json()
        names = []
        for entry in data:
            val = entry.get("name_value", "")
            if not val:
                continue
            # name_value may contain newline-delimited names
            for line in val.splitlines():
                line = line.strip()
                if line:
                    names.append(line)
        return names
    except Exception:
        return []

# --- domain normalization ---------------------------------------------------

def normalize_domain(name: str, strip_wild: bool = True, lower: bool = True) -> Optional[str]:
    if not name:
        return None
    name = name.strip()
    if strip_wild:
        if name.startswith("*."):
            name = name[2:]
        if name.startswith("\\*."):  # handle escaped star
            name = name[3:]
    # remove leading wildcard from multi-line crtsh forms
    name = name.lstrip("*. ")
    # remove trailing dots
    name = name.rstrip(".")
    if lower:
        name = name.lower()
    # make sure it contains a dot and valid suffix
    ext = tldextract.extract(name)
    if not ext.domain or not ext.suffix:
        return None
    return name

def normalize_many(names: Iterable[str], strip_wild: bool = True, lower: bool = True) -> List[str]:
    normed = []
    seen = set()
    for n in names:
        nd = normalize_domain(n, strip_wild, lower)
        if nd and nd not in seen:
            seen.add(nd)
            normed.append(nd)
    return sorted(normed)

# --- subprocess runner ------------------------------------------------------

def run_shell(cmd: str, timeout: int | None = None) -> Tuple[int, str, str, float, float, float]:
    """
    Run a shell command. Returncode, stdout, stderr, elapsed, cpu%, mem_mb.
    """
    start = time.time()
    try:
        proc = subprocess.Popen(
            cmd, shell=True, stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True
        )
        ps = psutil.Process(proc.pid)
    except Exception as e:
        return (127, "", str(e), 0.0, 0.0, 0.0)

    try:
        stdout, stderr = proc.communicate(timeout=timeout)
    except subprocess.TimeoutExpired:
        proc.kill()
        stdout, stderr = proc.communicate()
        return (124, stdout, "TimeoutExpired", time.time() - start, 0.0, 0.0)

    elapsed = time.time() - start
    try:
        cpu = ps.cpu_percent(interval=0.0)
        mem = ps.memory_info().rss / (1024 * 1024)
    except Exception:
        cpu = 0.0
        mem = 0.0
    return (proc.returncode, stdout, stderr, elapsed, cpu, mem)
9. core/runner.py
Parallel tool execution, error tracking.

python
Copy
Edit
# core/runner.py
from __future__ import annotations
import concurrent.futures as cf
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple
from core.logging_setup import get_logger
from core.utils import run_shell, tool_in_path, fetch_crtsh

logger = get_logger("runner")

class ToolResult:
    __slots__ = ("name","rc","stdout","stderr","elapsed","cpu","mem","outfile","skipped","reason")
    def __init__(self, name: str):
        self.name = name
        self.rc = -1
        self.stdout = ""
        self.stderr = ""
        self.elapsed = 0.0
        self.cpu = 0.0
        self.mem = 0.0
        self.outfile: Path | None = None
        self.skipped = False
        self.reason = ""

def _write_outfile(path: Path, data: str) -> None:
    path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    path.write_text(data, encoding="utf-8")

def run_subdomain_tool(name: str, cmd: str, target: str, outfile: Path, timeout: int) -> ToolResult:
    """
    Handle a subdomain tool. Supports special name 'crtsh_python' -> fetch_crtsh().
    """
    tr = ToolResult(name)
    tr.outfile = outfile

    # 'cmd' may be 'crtsh_python' marker
    if cmd == "crtsh_python":
        logger.info(f"Running CRT.sh query for {target}")
        data = fetch_crtsh(target)
        _write_outfile(outfile, "\n".join(data) + "\n")
        tr.rc = 0
        tr.stdout = f"Wrote {len(data)} lines from crt.sh"
        return tr

    # detect binary (first token)
    bin_name = cmd.split()[0]
    if not tool_in_path(bin_name):
        tr.skipped = True
        tr.reason = f"tool '{bin_name}' not in PATH"
        logger.warning(f"{name} skipped: {tr.reason}")
        return tr

    # fill cmd with target/outfile if placeholders present
    formatted_cmd = cmd.format(target=target, outfile=str(outfile))
    rc, out, err, elapsed, cpu, mem = run_shell(formatted_cmd, timeout=timeout)
    if out and not outfile.exists():
        # some tools print to stdout; capture
        _write_outfile(outfile, out)
    tr.rc = rc
    tr.stdout = out
    tr.stderr = err
    tr.elapsed = elapsed
    tr.cpu = cpu
    tr.mem = mem
    return tr

def run_subdomain_tools_parallel(
    tool_cfg: Dict[str, Dict], target: str, out_dir: Path, timeout: int, max_workers: int = 3
) -> Dict[str, ToolResult]:
    """
    Run all subdomain tools concurrently.
    Returns dict tool_name -> ToolResult
    """
    results: Dict[str, ToolResult] = {}
    futures = {}
    with cf.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=max_workers) as ex:
        for tname, meta in tool_cfg.items():
            outfile = out_dir / f"{tname}.txt"
            cmd = meta["cmd"]
            fut = ex.submit(run_subdomain_tool, tname, cmd, target, outfile, timeout)
            futures[fut] = tname
        for fut in cf.as_completed(futures):
            tname = futures[fut]
            tr = fut.result()
            results[tname] = tr
    return results

11. ui/progress.py

python
Copy

# ui/progress.py
from __future__ import annotations
import time
from rich.console import Console
from rich.progress import Progress, SpinnerColumn, TimeElapsedColumn, BarColumn, TextColumn

console = Console()

class PhaseProgress:
    def __init__(self, description: str, total: int):
        self.description = description
        self.total = total
        self._progress = Progress(
            SpinnerColumn(),
            TextColumn("[progress.description]{task.description}"),
            BarColumn(),
            TextColumn("{task.completed}/{task.total}"),
            TimeElapsedColumn(),
            console=console,
            transient=False,
        )
        self._task_id = None

    def __enter__(self):
        self._progress.__enter__()
        self._task_id = self._progress.add_task(self.description, total=self.total)
        return self

    def advance(self):
        self._progress.advance(self._task_id, 1)

    def update_desc(self, desc: str):
        self._progress.update(self._task_id, description=desc)

    def __exit__(self, exc_type, exc, tb):
        self._progress.__exit__(exc_type, exc, tb)
12. phases/subdomains.py
Phase runner: executes configured subdomain tools, aggregates, normalizes.

python
Copy
Edit
# phases/subdomains.py
from __future__ import annotations
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List
from core.logging_setup import get_logger
from core.utils import load_settings, normalize_many
from core.runner import run_subdomain_tools_parallel, ToolResult

logger = get_logger("phase.subdomains")

def run_phase_subdomains(
    target: str,
    tools_cfg: Dict[str, Dict],
    target_dir: Path,
    timeout: int,
    workers: int,
    resume: bool = False,
) -> Dict[str, ToolResult]:
    """
    Run all configured subdomain tools for `target`.
    Write per-tool output, merged raw, normalized aggregated file.
    Returns dict tool_name -> ToolResult
    """
    settings = load_settings()
    files_cfg = settings["filenames"]
    agg_file = target_dir / files_cfg["aggregated_subdomains"]
    merged_file = target_dir / files_cfg["merged_raw"]
    normalized_file = target_dir / files_cfg["normalized"]

    if resume and normalized_file.is_file():
        logger.info(f"[resume] using existing {normalized_file}")
        return {}

    # Ensure target dir exists
    target_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)

    # Run tools in parallel
    logger.info(f"Running subdomain tools against {target}")
    results = run_subdomain_tools_parallel(
        tools_cfg["tools"], target, target_dir, timeout=timeout, max_workers=workers
    )

    # Merge raw outputs
    raw_lines: List[str] = []
    for tname, tr in results.items():
        if tr.skipped:
            continue
        if tr.outfile and tr.outfile.is_file():
            raw_lines.extend(line.strip() for line in tr.outfile.read_text(encoding="utf-8").splitlines() if line.strip())
    merged_file.write_text("\n".join(raw_lines) + "\n", encoding="utf-8")

    # Normalize + dedupe
    normed = normalize_many(
        raw_lines,
        strip_wild=settings.get("strip_wildcard", True),
        lower=settings.get("lowercase", True),
    )
    agg_file.write_text("\n".join(normed) + "\n", encoding="utf-8")
    normalized_file.write_text("\n".join(normed) + "\n", encoding="utf-8")  # alias

    logger.info(f"Subdomain aggregation complete: {len(normed)} unique names.")

    return results

# NightOwl Phaseâ€‘1 (Subdomain OSINT Core)

This is the *first working milestone* of NightOwl â€” a modular bug bounty reconnaissance framework.

## Whatâ€™s Included
- CLI interface
- Subdomain tools: **Subfinder**, **Findomain**, **crt.sh**
- Parallel execution
- Error skipping & logging
- Result aggregation + normalization
- Resume support
- Rich TUI progress

# NightOwl Help (Phaseâ€‘1)

**Usage**
python3 main.py [--target DOMAIN | --targets-file FILE] [options]

markdown
Copy

**Options**
- `--target DOMAIN`       Single domain (example.com)
- `--targets-file FILE`   One domain per line
- `--phases subdomains`   Commaâ€‘separated phase list (default: subdomains)
- `--out-dir PATH`        Base output root (default from settings.yaml)
- `--resume`              Skip work if aggregated file exists
- `--save-json`           Write run summary JSON to target dir
- `--timeout N`           Override perâ€‘tool timeout seconds
- `--workers N`           Max parallel tools
- `--debug`               Verbose logging

**Examples**
python3 main.py --target uber.com --phases subdomains
python3 main.py --targets-file scope.txt --phases subdomains --workers 5
python3 main.py --target example.com --resume --save-json

15. main.py
Topâ€‘level orchestration for Phaseâ€‘1.

python
Copy
Edit
#!/usr/bin/env python3
# main.py
from __future__ import annotations
import argparse
import json
import sys
from pathlib import Path
from typing import List, Dict
from rich.console import Console

from ui.banner import print_banner
from ui.progress import console as rich_console, PhaseProgress
from core.logging_setup import get_logger
from core.utils import load_settings, load_tools_config
from core.state import StateManager
from phases.subdomains import run_phase_subdomains

console = Console()
logger = get_logger("main")

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def parse_args() -> argparse.Namespace:
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description="NightOwl Recon Phase-1 (Subdomain OSINT)",
        formatter_class=argparse.ArgumentDefaultsHelpFormatter,
    )
    g = ap.add_mutually_exclusive_group(required=True)
    g.add_argument("--target", help="Single target domain (example.com)")
    g.add_argument("--targets-file", help="File with one domain per line")
    ap.add_argument("--phases", default="subdomains", help="Comma-separated phase list")
    ap.add_argument("--out-dir", default=None, help="Override output root directory")
    ap.add_argument("--resume", action="store_true", help="Resume if data exists")
    ap.add_argument("--save-json", action="store_true", help="Save JSON summary")
    ap.add_argument("--timeout", type=int, default=None, help="Per-tool timeout seconds")
    ap.add_argument("--workers", type=int, default=None, help="Parallel tool runners")
    ap.add_argument("--debug", action="store_true", help="Verbose logging")
    return ap.parse_args()

def load_targets(args: argparse.Namespace) -> List[str]:
    if args.target:
        return [args.target.strip()]
    path = Path(args.targets_file)
    if not path.is_file():
        console.print(f"[red]Targets file not found: {path}[/red]")
        sys.exit(1)
    domains = [line.strip() for line in path.read_text().splitlines() if line.strip()]
    return domains

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def run_subdomains_wrapper(target: str, settings: Dict, tools_cfg: Dict, out_root: Path, args) -> Dict:
    # Setup target paths
    t_dir = out_root / target
    t_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)

    state = StateManager(t_dir)
    if args.resume:
        state.load()

    # Already done?
    if args.resume and state.is_completed("subdomains"):
        console.print(f"[yellow][resume] Subdomains phase previously completed for {target}[/yellow]")
        return {"skipped": True, "target": target}

    timeout = args.timeout if args.timeout else settings.get("tool_timeout", 600)
    workers = args.workers if args.workers else settings.get("concurrency", 3)

    console.print(f"[cyan]Running subdomains phase for [bold]{target}[/bold]...[/cyan]")
    with PhaseProgress("Subdomain tools", total=len(tools_cfg["tools"])) as pp:
        results = run_phase_subdomains(target, tools_cfg, t_dir, timeout, workers, resume=args.resume)
        # progress bar is coarse (one step per tool return)
        for _ in range(len(tools_cfg["tools"])):
            pp.advance()

    # Mark completion
    state.mark_phase("subdomains", "completed")

    # Build summary
    files_cfg = settings["filenames"]
    agg = t_dir / files_cfg["aggregated_subdomains"]
    count = sum(1 for _ in agg.read_text().splitlines() if _)
    tool_summary = {}
    for name, tr in results.items():
        tool_summary[name] = {
            "rc": tr.rc,
            "skipped": tr.skipped,
            "reason": tr.reason,
            "elapsed": tr.elapsed,
            "cpu": tr.cpu,
            "mem": tr.mem,
            "outfile": str(tr.outfile) if tr.outfile else None,
        }
    return {
        "target": target,
        "phase": "subdomains",
        "total_unique": count,
        "tools": tool_summary,
        "aggregated_file": str(agg),
    }

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def main():
    args = parse_args()
    print_banner()

    settings = load_settings()
    tools_cfg = load_tools_config()
    targets = load_targets(args)

    out_root = Path(args.out_dir) if args.out_dir else Path(settings["output_root"])
    out_root.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)

    all_summaries = []

    for target in targets:
        summary = run_subdomains_wrapper(target, settings, tools_cfg, out_root, args)
        all_summaries.append(summary)
        # Quick console summary:
        if summary.get("skipped"):
            console.print(f"[yellow]{target}: skipped (resume)[/yellow]")
        else:
            console.print(
                f"[green]{target}: {summary['total_unique']} unique subdomains."
            )

    if args.save_json:
        # Write combined summary
        out_file = out_root / "phase1_run_summary.json"
        out_file.write_text(json.dumps(all_summaries, indent=2), encoding="utf-8")
        console.print(f"[blue]Saved JSON summary to {out_file}[/blue]")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
